[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] advisor.started
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] Wor
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ker, before you go further, here is focused guidance.

**
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] Algorithmic insight — this is a 4-round Feistel, so the standard meet-in-the-middle / round-key
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  peeling attack applies. You do NOT need a true "linear" attack:**
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 

- The round keys `key[i]` are 32-bit but each is the deterministic `
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] expand()` of a 20-bit seed. So the actual unknown per round is only 20 bits. Brute-forcing one round at a time over
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  2^20 ≈ 1M candidates is trivial.
- Strategy: peel rounds from outside using known plaintext/
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ciphertext pairs. For each pair you can compute the input to round 0's F-function (from pl
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] aintext, after pre-mix) and you know the F output XOR relationship. Guess `seed0` (2
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ^20), check consistency across several pairs, keep survivors. Then peel that round off all
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  pairs and guess `seed1`, etc. With 32 pairs, false positives collapse to one cand
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] idate per round quickly.
- Alternatively, since each seed is only 20 bits and
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  there are 4 of them, a layered guess (1M per layer, 4 layers) is f
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ast in C. Don't try 2^80 all at once.

**Concrete recommendation
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] :**
1. Port the cipher to a small C program (reuse feal.c's ex
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] act `expand`, `f_function`, `g_function`, round structure — copy verbatim to avoid bugs). C will
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  be far faster than Python for the 2^20 loops.
2. Implement round-peeling: write a function that, given a cand
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] idate seed for the outer round, partially decrypts/encrypts all pairs and checks the half-block
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  invariant of a Feistel round.
3. Verify each recovered seed against ALL 32 pairs (full encrypt ==
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  ciphertext) before trusting it.

**Important correctness checks:**
- Note the byte extraction in `f_function` is little-endian
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  within the loop (`x[i] = input & 0xFF; input >>= 8`), and recombination u
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ses `y[i] << (8*i)`. Match this exactly.
- Note pre-round mix `right ^= left`
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] , 4 rounds, then post-round `left ^= right`, then `merge(right,left)` (swapped). Get
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  the swap right — that's the easiest place to make an off-by-one error.
- pairs.txt and ciphertexts.txt
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  are **decimal** integers (the decrypt.c uses `%lu`). Read them as decimal, not hex.
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 

**Final validation before declaring done:**
- Once you find the 4 seeds, run `./decrypt ci
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] phertexts.txt s0 s1 s2 s3 > /app/plaintexts.txt` and confirm: encrypting
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  each recovered plaintext with `./feal` reproduces the ciphertext for at least a few entries, and that all 32 known
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  pairs check out with these seeds.
- Make sure output format of plaintexts.txt matches what's
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  expected (decimal, one per line — the decrypt binary already does this).

**One process note:** your JSON keeps triggering "extra text" warnings even
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  though I don't see stray text — ensure nothing (no leading/
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] trailing characters, no markdown fences) surrounds the raw JSON object.

Proceed: write the C att
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ack now, recover the 4 seeds, then generate plaintexts.txt with
[tr-stream call-0008:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  the existing decrypt binary.
